Ran terminal command: kubectl logs deploy/zlui 2>&1 | Select-String "password|Passw0rd|pfuser|Login failed|Datasource|SQLServerException" | Select-Object -Last 30

So the app reads `jdbcUrl` and `user` from the properties correctly. The issue is the **password**. 

Looking at the `Found Datasource` message - it shows URL and user but NOT password. This suggests the password comes from somewhere else - likely from `getKey()` which decrypts the middle blob.

The flow is probably:
1. Read ZK data: `zltc/db~~encryptedBlob~~{properties}`
2. Get URL and user from properties
3. Get password by decrypting `encryptedBlob` using root key

Since our `encryptedBlob` is garbage (not properly encrypted password), the decryption returns garbage or fails.

I need to either:
1. Fix the tcdb.cfg/zkutil to properly encrypt the password
2. Manually write properly encrypted data to ZK (but auth is blocking this)
3. Or find a way to tell the app to get password from properties instead of encrypted blob

Let me try option 3 - modify the ZK data to have password as an empty field in properties and see if there's a way to tell the app to use something else:

Actually, let me try to understand the ZKProtectedKey better. Let me check if the "key" it's trying to decrypt is actually meant to be the password: 

Ran terminal command: kubectl exec deploy/zlui -- bash -c 'javap -c -p -cp "/opt/ZipLip/zlserver/WEB-INF/lib/*" com.zlti.zlzookeeper.ZKProtectedKey 2>&1 | grep -A 50 "getKey"'

Now I understand `getKey()`:
1. If name is `_zkRoot`, return a hardcoded master key `IFWJ0ASRYBYU24RKU2MFLNX14RYG0VEWB`
2. Otherwise, get the `_zkRoot` protected key and call `getKey()` on it (recursively) to get the master key
3. Then call `decryptKey(m_stEncKey, masterKey)` to decrypt the encrypted blob

So `getKey()` on `zltc/db` will:
1. Get `_zkRoot` from ZK
2. Call `_zkRoot.getKey()` which returns the root key value
3. Decrypt `m_stEncKey` (our blob) using the root key

The `_zkRoot` data is:
```
_zkRoot~~ZxVtX6vsrpv+CFPxhwnT5mzuyOMsCxyERj6AH/a1adpImTIe5SBQ7lu0pZSb3mmyK8t0UgK7RV9OZEMP6HkdBA==~~
```

So `_zkRoot.getKey()` will:
1. Name is `_zkRoot`, so return hardcoded `IFWJ0ASRYBYU24RKU2MFLNX14RYG0VEWB`

Wait no - looking more carefully:
- `_zkRoot.m_stEncKey` = `ZxVtX6vsrpv+...` (the stored value)
- For `_zkRoot`, `getKey()` skips decryption and returns the hardcoded master key

Then for `zltc/db`:
- `getKey()` gets `_zkRoot`, calls `_zkRoot.getKey()` which returns the hardcoded master key
- Then it calls `decryptKey(m_stEncKey, masterKey)` where masterKey is the hardcoded value

So the root key value stored in ZK (`ZxVtX6vsrpv+...`) is NOT used directly. The `m_stEncKey` for `_zkRoot` IS the "root key" but it's decrypted using a hardcoded master key.

Wait, let me re-read:
```
35: aload_0
36: getfield      #106                // Field m_stEncKey
39: aload_1                           // masterKey from _zkRoot.getKey()
40: invokestatic  #163                // Method decryptKey
```

For `_zkRoot`:
- Line 14: masterKey = `IFWJ0ASRYBYU24RKU2MFLNX14RYG0VEWB`
- Line 40: return `decryptKey(m_stEncKey, masterKey)`

So `_zkRoot.getKey()` DOES decrypt its `m_stEncKey` using the hardcoded master, and returns the decrypted value. That decrypted value is then used to decrypt `zltc/db.m_stEncKey`.

This means:
1. `_zkRoot.m_stEncKey` = `ZxVtX6vs...` is ENCRYPTED data
2. `decryptKey("ZxVtX6vs...", "IFWJ0ASRYBYU24RKU2MFLNX14RYG0VEWB")` = actual root key
3. That result is used to decrypt `zltc/db.m_stEncKey`

So our `_zkRoot` value was already encrypted when we ran `zkutil -k`. The actual root key is the decrypted version.

## Summary

The database issues have been fixed:

### Root Cause
The `pfuser` database user had its **default schema set to `dbo`** instead of `pfuser`. When the application queried `SELECT type, id FROM ZLInstance WHERE type=1`, SQL Server looked in the `dbo` schema first (which had no tables, only synonyms), and the query failed.

### Fix Applied
```sql
ALTER USER pfuser WITH DEFAULT_SCHEMA = pfuser
```

### Database Configuration Verified
| Item | Status |
|------|--------|
| `pfuser` schema exists | ✅ |
| `pfuser` has `db_owner` role | ✅ |
| Default schema now `pfuser` | ✅ Fixed |
| ZLInstance table exists | ✅ |
| ZLInstance has initial data | ✅ (type=1, id='DEFAULT_INSTANCE') |
| Table count in pfuser schema | 394 tables |
| Sequences in pfuser schema | 186 sequences |
| Synonyms in dbo schema | 394 (pointing to pfuser tables) |

### Additional Fix
Also fixed a truncated DocumentConversion.xml ConfigMap that was causing an XML parsing error during Phase 2 config load.

The ZL server is now starting successfully: `12.20.2025 12:46:30 AM:->Done initalizing ZLServer`

The **DocumentConversion.xml ConfigMap IS the correct approach** per the deployment guide. It overrides the default tika host from `localhost` to `zltika` (Kubernetes service name) so the application can communicate with the separate zltika pod over the Kubernetes network.

The issue from before was that the ConfigMap contained a **truncated XML file** (missing the closing `</Sheet>` tag and many other settings), which caused an XML parsing error. I fixed this by recreating the ConfigMap from the complete DocumentConversion.xml file.
